Course Week 4: Good Programming Practices Problem Set 4 Computer Choosing a Word and Playing a Hand
<div class="xblock xblock-student_view xblock-student_view-vertical" data-runtime-class="LmsRuntime" data-init="VerticalStudentView" data-course-id="course-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017" data-request-token="6a44223e63e511e7b0fc065085eb7ade" data-runtime-version="1" data-usage-id="block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@vertical+block@bb51d959281e431bb64ac02f5a3ff580" data-block-type="vertical"> <h2 class="hd hd-2 unit-title">Introduction</h2> <div class="bookmark-button-wrapper"> <button class="btn btn-link bookmark-button " aria-pressed="false" data-bookmark-id="infra1515,block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@vertical+block@bb51d959281e431bb64ac02f5a3ff580" data-bookmarks-api-url="/api/bookmarks/v1/bookmarks/"> <span class="bookmark-text">Bookmark this page</span> </button> </div> <div class="vert-mod"> <div class="vert vert-0" data-id="block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@html+block@eeb64a67e52e4f3e80656b9233204f25"> <div class="xblock xblock-student_view xblock-student_view-html xmodule_display xmodule_HtmlModule" data-runtime-class="LmsRuntime" data-init="XBlockToXModuleShim" data-block-type="html" data-request-token="6a44223e63e511e7b0fc065085eb7ade" data-runtime-version="1" data-usage-id="block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@html+block@eeb64a67e52e4f3e80656b9233204f25" data-type="HTMLModule" data-course-id="course-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017"> <script type="json/xblock-args" class="xblock-json-init-args"> {"xmodule-type": "HTMLModule"} </script> <div id="edx-notes-wrapper-140832633721415037088966197164913573466" class="edx-notes-wrapper"> <div class="edx-notes-wrapper-content"><p>In this problem set, you'll implement <em>two</em> versions of a wordgame!</p> <p>Don't be intimidated by the length of this problem set. There is a lot of reading, but it can be done with a reasonable amount of thinking and coding. It'll be helpful if you start this problem set a few days before it is due!</p> <p>Let's begin by describing the 6.00 wordgame: This game is a lot like Scrabble or Words With Friends, if you've played those. Letters are dealt to players, who then construct one or more words out of their letters. Each <strong>valid</strong> word receives a score, based on the length of the word and the letters in that word.</p> <p>The rules of the game are as follows:</p> <dl><dt><strong>Dealing</strong></dt><dd> <ul> <li> <p>A player is dealt a hand of <em>n</em> letters chosen at random (assume <em>n=7</em> for now).</p> </li> <li> <p>The player arranges the hand into as many words as they want out of the letters, using each letter at most once.</p> </li> <li> <p>Some letters may remain unused (these won't be scored).</p> </li> </ul> </dd><dt><strong>Scoring</strong></dt><dd> <ul> <li> <p>The score for the hand is the sum of the scores for each word formed.</p> </li> <li> <p>The score for a word is the sum of the points for letters in the word, multiplied by the length of the word, plus 50 points if all <em>n</em> letters are used on the first word created.</p> </li> <li> <p>Letters are scored as in Scrabble; A is worth 1, B is worth 3, C is worth 3, D is worth 2, E is worth 1, and so on. We have defined the dictionary <code>SCRABBLE_LETTER_VALUES</code> that maps each lowercase letter to its Scrabble letter value.</p> </li> <li> <p>For example, 'weed' would be worth 32 points ((4+1+1+2) for the four letters, then multiply by <code>len('weed')</code> to get (4+1+1+2)*4 = 32). Be sure to check that the hand actually has 1 'w', 2 'e's, and 1 'd' before scoring the word!</p> </li> <li> <p>As another example, if <em>n</em>=7 and you make the word 'waybill' on the first try, it would be worth 155 points (the base score for 'waybill' is (4+1+4+3+1+1+1)*7=105, plus an additional 50 point bonus for using all <em>n</em> letters).</p> </li> </ul> </dd></dl> <section class="hints"> <h3>Sample Output</h3> <div class="collapsible"><header><a id="ht1l" href="#">Here is how the game output will look!</a></header> <section id="ht1"> <pre><code> Loading word list from file... 83667 words loaded. Enter n to deal a new hand, r to replay the last hand, or e to end game: n Current Hand: p z u t t t o Enter word, or a "." to indicate that you are finished: tot "tot" earned 9 points. Total: 9 points Current Hand: p z u t Enter word, or a "." to indicate that you are finished: . Total score: 9 points. Enter n to deal a new hand, r to replay the last hand, or e to end game: r Current Hand: p z u t t t o Enter word, or a "." to indicate that you are finished: top "top" earned 15 points. Total: 15 points Current Hand: z u t t Enter word, or a "." to indicate that you are finished: tu Invalid word, please try again. Current Hand: z u t t Enter word, or a "." to indicate that you are finished: . Total score: 15 points. Enter n to deal a new hand, r to replay the last hand, or e to end game: n Current Hand: a q w f f i p Enter word, or a "." to indicate that you are finished: paw "paw" earned 24 points. Total: 24 points Current Hand: q f f i Enter word, or a "." to indicate that you are finished: qi "qi" earned 22 points. Total: 46 points Current Hand: f f Enter word, or a "." to indicate that you are finished: . Total score: 46 points. Total: 99 points Run out of letters. Total score: 99 points. Enter n to deal a new hand, r to replay the last hand, or e to end game: e </code></pre> </section> </div> </section> <p></p> <p></p></div> </div> <script type="text/javascript"> (function (require) { Extract the files from the zip folder and make sure to save <i>all</i> the files &nbsp;- <code>ps4a.py</code>, <code>ps4b.py</code>, <code>test_ps4a.py</code> and <code>words.txt</code> - in the <b>same folder</b>. If you don't follow this instruction, you may end up with issues because the files for this problem set depend on one another.</p> </li> <li> <p>Run the file <code>ps4a.py</code>, without making any modifications to it, in order to ensure that everything is set up correctly (this means, open the file in IDLE, and use the Run command to load the file into the interpreter). The code we have given you loads a list of valid words from a file and then calls the <code>playGame</code> function. You will implement the functions it needs in order to work. If everything is okay, after a small delay, you should see the following printed out:</p> <pre><code> Loading word list from file... 83667 words loaded. playGame not yet implemented. </code></pre> <br /> <p>If you see an <code>IOError</code> instead (e.g., "No such file or directory"), you should change the value of the <code>WORDLIST_FILENAME</code> constant (defined near the top of the file) to the <strong>complete pathname</strong> for the file <code>words.txt</code> (This will vary based on where you saved the files).</p> <p>For example, if you saved all the files including this <code>words.txt</code> in the directory "C:/Users/Ana/6001x/PS4" change the line:&nbsp;</p> <p><code style="background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 16px;">WORDLIST_FILENAME = "words.txt"</code>&nbsp; to something like&nbsp;<br /><code style="background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 16px;">WORDLIST_FILENAME = "C:/Users/Ana/6001x/PS4/words.txt"</code><span style="line-height: 25.6px;">&nbsp;</span><br />Windows users, if you are copying the file path from Windows Explorer, you will have to change the backslashes to forward slashes.</p> </li> <li> <p>The file <code>ps4a.py</code> has a number of already implemented functions you can use while writing up your solution. You can ignore the code between the following comments, though you should read and understand how to use each helper function by reading the docstrings:</p> <pre><code># ----------------------------------- # Helper code # You don't need to understand this helper code, # but you will have to know how to use the functions # (so be sure to read the docstrings!) . . . # (end of helper code) # ----------------------------------- <br /><br /></code></pre> </li> <li> <p>This problem set is structured so that you will write a number of modular functions and then glue them together to form the complete word playing game. Instead of waiting until the entire game is <em>ready</em>, you should test each function you write, individually, before moving on. This approach is known as <em>unit testing</em>, and it will help you debug your code.</p> </li> </ol> <p>We have provided several test functions to get you started. After you've written each new function, unit test by running the file <code>test_ps4a.py</code> to check your work.</p> <p>If your code passes the unit tests you will see a <code>SUCCESS</code> message; otherwise you will see a <code>FAILURE</code> message. These tests aren't exhaustive. You will want to test your code in other ways too.</p> <p>Try running <code>test_ps4a.py</code> now (before you modify the <code>ps4a.py</code> skeleton). <div class="xblock xblock-student_view xblock-student_view-vertical" data-runtime-class="LmsRuntime" data-init="VerticalStudentView" data-course-id="course-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017" data-request-token="6a44223e63e511e7b0fc065085eb7ade" data-runtime-version="1" data-usage-id="block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@vertical+block@544d6c6b87ad4aea8034d5e0802aa37d" data-block-type="vertical"> <h2 class="hd hd-2 unit-title">Problem 1 - Word Scores</h2> <div class="bookmark-button-wrapper"> <button class="btn btn-link bookmark-button " aria-pressed="false" data-bookmark-id="infra1515,block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@vertical+block@544d6c6b87ad4aea8034d5e0802aa37d" data-bookmarks-api-url="/api/bookmarks/v1/bookmarks/"> <span class="bookmark-text">Bookmark this page</span> </button> </div> <div class="vert-mod"> <div class="vert vert-0" data-id="block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@problem+block@82ca4ccb5890466d80f6b393eb681a32"> <div class="xblock xblock-student_view xblock-student_view-problem xmodule_display xmodule_CapaModule" data-runtime-class="LmsRuntime" data-init="XBlockToXModuleShim" data-block-type="problem" data-request-token="6a44223e63e511e7b0fc065085eb7ade" data-runtime-version="1" data-usage-id="block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@problem+block@82ca4ccb5890466d80f6b393eb681a32" data-type="Problem" data-course-id="course-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017"> <script type="json/xblock-args" class="xblock-json-init-args"> {"xmodule-type": "Problem"} </script> <div id="problem_82ca4ccb5890466d80f6b393eb681a32" class="problems-wrapper" role="group" aria-labelledby="82ca4ccb5890466d80f6b393eb681a32-problem-title" data-problem-id="block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@problem+block@82ca4ccb5890466d80f6b393eb681a32" data-url="/courses/course-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017/xblock/block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@problem+block@82ca4ccb5890466d80f6b393eb681a32/handler/xmodule_handler" data-problem-score="10.0" data-problem-total-possible="10.0" data-attempts-used="1" data-content=" &lt;h3 class=&#34;hd hd-3 problem-header&#34; id=&#34;82ca4ccb5890466d80f6b393eb681a32-problem-title&#34; aria-describedby=&#34;block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@problem+block@82ca4ccb5890466d80f6b393eb681a32-problem-progress&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34;&gt; Problem 1 - Word Scores &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem-progress&#34; id=&#34;block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@problem+block@82ca4ccb5890466d80f6b393eb681a32-problem-progress&#34;&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem&#34;&gt; &lt;div&gt;&lt;style media=&#34;all&#34; type=&#34;text/css&#34;/&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;p&gt;The first step is to implement some code that allows us to calculate the score for a single word. The function &lt;code&gt;getWordScore&lt;/code&gt; should accept as input a string of lowercase letters (a &lt;em&gt;word&lt;/em&gt;) and return the integer score for that word, using the game&#39;s scoring rules. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;section class=&#34;hints&#34;&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;ht1l&#34;&gt;A Reminder of the Scoring Rules&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;ht1&#34;&gt;&lt;dt&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Scoring&lt;/strong&gt;&lt;/dt&gt;&lt;dd&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;The score for the hand is the sum of the scores for each word formed.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;The score for a word is the sum of the points for letters in the word, multiplied by the length of the word, plus 50 points if all &lt;em&gt;n&lt;/em&gt; letters are used on the first word created.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Letters are scored as in Scrabble; A is worth 1, B is worth 3, C is worth 3, D is worth 2, E is worth 1, and so on. We have defined the dictionary &lt;code&gt;SCRABBLE_LETTER_VALUES&lt;/code&gt; that maps each lowercase letter to its Scrabble letter value.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;For example, &#39;weed&#39; would be worth 32 points ((4+1+1+2) for the four letters, then multiply by &lt;code&gt;len(&#39;weed&#39;)&lt;/code&gt; to get (4+1+1+2)*4 = 32). Be sure to check that the hand actually has 1 &#39;w&#39;, 2 &#39;e&#39;s, and 1 &#39;d&#39; before scoring the word!&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;As another example, if &lt;em&gt;n&lt;/em&gt;=7 and you make the word &#39;waybill&#39; on the first try, it would be worth 155 points (the base score for &#39;waybill&#39; is (4+1+4+3+1+1+1)*7=105, plus an additional 50 point bonus for using all &lt;em&gt;n&lt;/em&gt; letters).&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;/dd&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;br/&gt;&lt;h2&gt;Hints&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;You may assume that the input &lt;code&gt;word&lt;/code&gt; is always either a string of lowercase letters, or the empty string &lt;code&gt;&#34;&#34;&lt;/code&gt;. &lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;You will want to use the &lt;code&gt;SCRABBLE_LETTER_VALUES&lt;/code&gt; dictionary defined at the top of &lt;code&gt;ps4a.py&lt;/code&gt;. You should not change its value.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt; Do &lt;strong&gt;not&lt;/strong&gt; assume that there are always 7 letters in a hand! The parameter &lt;code&gt;n&lt;/code&gt; is the number of letters required for a bonus score (the maximum number of letters in the hand). Our goal is to keep the code modular - if you want to try playing your word game with &lt;em&gt;n=10&lt;/em&gt; or &lt;em&gt;n=4&lt;/em&gt;, you will be able to do it by simply changing the value of &lt;code&gt;HAND_SIZE&lt;/code&gt;!&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Testing:&lt;/strong&gt; If this function is implemented properly, and you run &lt;code&gt;test_ps4a.py&lt;/code&gt;, you should see that the &lt;code&gt;test_getWordScore()&lt;/code&gt; tests pass. Also test your implementation of &lt;code&gt;getWordScore&lt;/code&gt;, using some reasonable English words.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;Fill in the code for &lt;code&gt;getWordScore&lt;/code&gt; in &lt;code&gt;ps4a.py&lt;/code&gt; and be sure you&#39;ve passed the appropriate tests in &lt;code&gt;test_ps4a.py&lt;/code&gt; before pasting your function definition here.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;wrapper-problem-response&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34; aria-label=&#34;Question 1&#34; role=&#34;group&#34;&gt;&lt;div id=&#34;textbox_82ca4ccb5890466d80f6b393eb681a32_2_1&#34; class=&#34;capa_inputtype textbox cminput&#34;&gt;&lt;label class=&#34;sr problem-group-label&#34; for=&#34;cm-textarea-82ca4ccb5890466d80f6b393eb681a32_2_1&#34;&gt;Code Editor&lt;/label&gt;&lt;textarea rows=&#34;30&#34; cols=&#34;70&#34; name=&#34;input_82ca4ccb5890466d80f6b393eb681a32_2_1&#34; aria-label=&#34;python editor&#34; aria-describedby=&#34;answer_82ca4ccb5890466d80f6b393eb681a32_2_1&#34; id=&#34;input_82ca4ccb5890466d80f6b393eb681a32_2_1&#34; tabindex=&#34;0&#34; data-mode=&#34;python&#34; data-tabsize=&#34;4&#34; data-linenums=&#34;true&#34;&gt;def getWordScore(word, n): &#34;&#34;&#34; Returns the score for a word. Assumes the word is a valid word. The score for a word is the sum of the points for letters in the word, multiplied by the length of the word, PLUS 50 points if all n letters are used on the first turn. Letters are scored as in Scrabble; A is worth 1, B is worth 3, C is worth 3, D is worth 2, E is worth 1, and so on (see SCRABBLE_LETTER_VALUES) word: string (lowercase letters) n: integer (HAND_SIZE; i.e., hand size required for additional points) returns: int &amp;gt;= 0 &#34;&#34;&#34; score = 0 for ch in word: score += SCRABBLE_LETTER_VALUES[ch] score = score * len(word) if n == len(word): return score + 50 else: return score &lt;/textarea&gt;&lt;span class=&#34;cm-editor-exit-message capa-message&#34; id=&#34;cm-editor-exit-message-82ca4ccb5890466d80f6b393eb681a32_2_1&#34;&gt; Press ESC then TAB or click outside of the code editor to exit &lt;/span&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;grader-status&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34;&gt;&lt;span class=&#34;status correct&#34; id=&#34;status_82ca4ccb5890466d80f6b393eb681a32_2_1&#34; data-tooltip=&#34;This answer is correct.&#34;&gt;&lt;span class=&#34;sr&#34;&gt;correct&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&#34;status-icon&#34; Dealing with Hands &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem-progress&#34; id=&#34;block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@problem+block@00d6ec9ae9e74c38b9ad4833c9cca91c-problem-progress&#34;&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem&#34;&gt; &lt;div&gt;&lt;style media=&#34;all&#34; type=&#34;text/css&#34;/&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;span style=&#34;color: #ff0000;&#34;&gt;**Please read this problem entirely!!**&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/b&gt; The majority of this problem consists of learning how to read code, which is an incredibly useful and important skill. At the end, you will implement a short function. Be sure to take your time on this problem - it may seem easy, but reading someone else&#39;s code can be challenging and this is an important exercise. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;br/&gt;&lt;h2&gt;Representing hands&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;A &lt;b&gt;hand&lt;/b&gt; is the set of letters held by a player during the game. The player is initially dealt a set of random letters. For example, the player could start out with the following hand: &lt;strong&gt;&lt;code&gt;a, q, l, m, u, i, l&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;. In our program, a hand will be represented as a dictionary: the keys are (lowercase) letters and the values are the number of times the particular letter is repeated in that hand. For example, the above hand would be represented as:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;pre&gt;hand = {&#39;a&#39;:1, &#39;q&#39;:1, &#39;l&#39;:2, &#39;m&#39;:1, &#39;u&#39;:1, &#39;i&#39;:1} &lt;/pre&gt;&lt;p&gt;Notice how the repeated letter &lt;code&gt;&#39;l&#39;&lt;/code&gt; is represented. Remember that with a dictionary, the usual way to access a value is &lt;code&gt;hand[&#39;a&#39;]&lt;/code&gt;, where &lt;code&gt;&#39;a&#39;&lt;/code&gt; is the key we want to find. However, this only works if the key is in the dictionary; otherwise, we get a &lt;code&gt;KeyError&lt;/code&gt;. To avoid this, we can use the call &lt;code&gt;hand.get(&#39;a&#39;,0)&lt;/code&gt;. This is the &#34;safe&#34; way to access a value if we are not sure the key is in the dictionary. &lt;code&gt;d.get(key,default)&lt;/code&gt; returns the value for &lt;code&gt;key&lt;/code&gt; if &lt;code&gt;key&lt;/code&gt; is in the dictionary &lt;code&gt;d&lt;/code&gt;, else &lt;code&gt;default&lt;/code&gt;. If &lt;code&gt;default&lt;/code&gt; is not given, it returns &lt;code&gt;None&lt;/code&gt;, so that this method never raises a &lt;code&gt;KeyError&lt;/code&gt;. For example:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&amp;gt;&amp;gt;&amp;gt; hand[&#39;e&#39;] Traceback (most recent call last): File &#34;&amp;lt;stdin&amp;gt;&#34;, line 1, in &amp;lt;module&amp;gt; KeyError: &#39;e&#39; &amp;gt;&amp;gt;&amp;gt; hand.get(&#39;e&#39;, 0) 0&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;h2&gt;Converting words into dictionary representation&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;One useful function we&#39;ve defined for you is &lt;code&gt;getFrequencyDict&lt;/code&gt;, defined near the top of &lt;code&gt;ps4a.py&lt;/code&gt;. When given a string of letters as an input, it returns a dictionary where the keys are letters and the values are the number of times that letter is represented in the input string. For example:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&amp;gt;&amp;gt;&amp;gt; getFrequencyDict(&#34;hello&#34;) {&#39;h&#39;: 1, &#39;e&#39;: 1, &#39;l&#39;: 2, &#39;o&#39;: 1}&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;p&gt;As you can see, this is the same kind of dictionary we use to represent hands.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h2&gt;Displaying a hand&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;Given a hand represented as a dictionary, we want to display it in a user-friendly way. We have provided the implementation for this in the &lt;code&gt;displayHand&lt;/code&gt; function. Take a few minutes right now to read through this function carefully and understand what it does and how it works.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h2&gt;Generating a random hand&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;The hand a player is dealt is a set of letters chosen at random. We provide you with the implementation of a function that generates this random hand, &lt;code&gt;dealHand&lt;/code&gt;. The function takes as input a positive integer &lt;code&gt;n&lt;/code&gt;, and returns a new object, a hand containing &lt;code&gt;n&lt;/code&gt; lowercase letters. Again, take a few minutes (right now!) to read through this function carefully and understand what it does and how it works.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h2&gt;Removing letters from a hand (you implement this)&lt;/h2&gt;&lt;p&gt;The player starts with a hand, a set of letters. As the player spells out words, letters from this set are used up. For example, the player could start out with the following hand: &lt;strong&gt;&lt;code&gt;a, q, l, m, u, i, l&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;. The player could choose to spell the word &lt;strong&gt;&lt;code&gt;quail&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/strong&gt; . This would leave the following letters in the player&#39;s hand: &lt;strong&gt;&lt;code&gt;l, m&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;. Your task is to implement the function &lt;code&gt;updateHand&lt;/code&gt;, which takes in two inputs - a &lt;code&gt;hand&lt;/code&gt; and a &lt;code&gt;word&lt;/code&gt; (string). &lt;code&gt;updateHand&lt;/code&gt; uses letters from the hand to spell the word, and then returns a copy of the &lt;code&gt;hand&lt;/code&gt;, containing only the letters remaining. For example:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&amp;gt;&amp;gt;&amp;gt; hand = {&#39;a&#39;:1, &#39;q&#39;:1, &#39;l&#39;:2, &#39;m&#39;:1, &#39;u&#39;:1, &#39;i&#39;:1} &amp;gt;&amp;gt;&amp;gt; displayHand(hand) # Implemented for you a q l l m u i &amp;gt;&amp;gt;&amp;gt; hand = updateHand(hand, &#39;quail&#39;) # You implement this function! &amp;gt;&amp;gt;&amp;gt; hand {&#39;a&#39;:0, &#39;q&#39;:0, &#39;l&#39;:1, &#39;m&#39;:1, &#39;u&#39;:0, &#39;i&#39;:0} &amp;gt;&amp;gt;&amp;gt; displayHand(hand) l m &lt;/pre&gt;&lt;p&gt;Implement the &lt;code&gt;updateHand&lt;/code&gt; function. Make sure this function has no side effects: i.e., it must not mutate the hand passed in. Before pasting your function definition here, be sure you&#39;ve passed the appropriate tests in &lt;code&gt;test_ps4a.py&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;section class=&#34;hints&#34;&gt;&lt;h3&gt;Hints&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;ht2&#34;&gt;Testing&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;ht2&#34;&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Testing:&lt;/strong&gt; Make sure the &lt;code&gt;test_updateHand()&lt;/code&gt; tests pass. You will also want to test your implementation of &lt;code&gt;updateHand&lt;/code&gt; with some reasonable inputs.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;ht1&#34;&gt;Copying Dictionaries&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;ht1&#34;&gt;&lt;p&gt;You may wish to review the &#34;.copy&#34; method of Python dictionaries (review this and other Python dictionary methods &lt;a href=&#34;http://docs.python.org/library/stdtypes.html#mapping-types-dict&#34; target=&#34;_blank&#34;&gt; here&lt;/a&gt;). &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;br/&gt;&lt;p&gt;Your implementation of updateHand should be short (ours is 4 lines of code). It does not need to call any helper functions.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;wrapper-problem-response&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34; aria-label=&#34;Question 1&#34; role=&#34;group&#34;&gt;&lt;div id=&#34;textbox_00d6ec9ae9e74c38b9ad4833c9cca91c_2_1&#34; class=&#34;capa_inputtype textbox cminput&#34;&gt;&lt;label class=&#34;sr problem-group-label&#34; for=&#34;cm-textarea-00d6ec9ae9e74c38b9ad4833c9cca91c_2_1&#34;&gt;Code Editor&lt;/label&gt;&lt;textarea rows=&#34;30&#34; cols=&#34;70&#34; name=&#34;input_00d6ec9ae9e74c38b9ad4833c9cca91c_2_1&#34; aria-label=&#34;python editor&#34; aria-describedby=&#34;answer_00d6ec9ae9e74c38b9ad4833c9cca91c_2_1&#34; id=&#34;input_00d6ec9ae9e74c38b9ad4833c9cca91c_2_1&#34; tabindex=&#34;0&#34; data-mode=&#34;python&#34; data-tabsize=&#34;4&#34; data-linenums=&#34;true&#34;&gt;def updateHand(hand, word): &#34;&#34;&#34; Assumes that &#39;hand&#39; has all the letters in word. In other words, this assumes that however many times a letter appears in &#39;word&#39;, &#39;hand&#39; has at least as many of that letter in it. Updates the hand: uses up the letters in the given word and returns the new hand, without those letters in it. Has no side effects: does not modify hand. word: string hand: dictionary (string -&amp;gt; int) returns: dictionary (string -&amp;gt; int) &#34;&#34;&#34; handCopy = hand.copy() for ch in word: if ch Valid Words</h2> <div class="bookmark-button-wrapper"> <button class="btn btn-link bookmark-button " aria-pressed="false" data-bookmark-id="infra1515,block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@vertical+block@84580e141127478ca53d4f29dc7df6f7" data-bookmarks-api-url="/api/bookmarks/v1/bookmarks/"> <span class="bookmark-text">Bookmark this page</span> </button> </div> <div class="vert-mod"> <div class="vert vert-0" data-id="block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@problem+block@78fd656ca17b446e8096a6ab04198382"> <div class="xblock xblock-student_view xblock-student_view-problem xmodule_display xmodule_CapaModule" data-runtime-class="LmsRuntime" data-init="XBlockToXModuleShim" data-block-type="problem" data-request-token="6a44223e63e511e7b0fc065085eb7ade" data-runtime-version="1" data-usage-id="block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@problem+block@78fd656ca17b446e8096a6ab04198382" data-type="Problem" data-course-id="course-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017"> <script type="json/xblock-args" class="xblock-json-init-args"> {"xmodule-type": "Problem"} </script> <div id="problem_78fd656ca17b446e8096a6ab04198382" class="problems-wrapper" role="group" aria-labelledby="78fd656ca17b446e8096a6ab04198382-problem-title" data-problem-id="block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@problem+block@78fd656ca17b446e8096a6ab04198382" data-url="/courses/course-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017/xblock/block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@problem+block@78fd656ca17b446e8096a6ab04198382/handler/xmodule_handler" data-problem-score="10.0" data-problem-total-possible="10.0" data-attempts-used="1" data-content=" &lt;h3 class=&#34;hd hd-3 problem-header&#34; id=&#34;78fd656ca17b446e8096a6ab04198382-problem-title&#34; aria-describedby=&#34;block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@problem+block@78fd656ca17b446e8096a6ab04198382-problem-progress&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34;&gt; Problem 3 - Valid Words &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem-progress&#34; id=&#34;block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@problem+block@78fd656ca17b446e8096a6ab04198382-problem-progress&#34;&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem&#34;&gt; &lt;div&gt;&lt;style media=&#34;all&#34; type=&#34;text/css&#34;/&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;p&gt;At this point, we have written code to generate a random hand and display that hand to the user. We can also ask the user for a word (Python&#39;s &lt;code&gt;input&lt;/code&gt;) and score the word (using your &lt;code&gt;getWordScore&lt;/code&gt;). However, at this point we have not written any code to verify that a word given by a player obeys the rules of the game. A &lt;em&gt;valid&lt;/em&gt; word is in the word list; &lt;strong&gt;and&lt;/strong&gt; it is composed entirely of letters from the current hand. Implement the &lt;code&gt;isValidWord&lt;/code&gt; function.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Testing:&lt;/strong&gt; Make sure the &lt;code&gt;test_isValidWord&lt;/code&gt; tests pass. In addition, you will want to test your implementation by calling it multiple times on the same hand - what should the correct behavior be? Additionally, the empty string (&lt;code&gt;&#39;&#39;&lt;/code&gt;) is not a valid word - if you code this function correctly, you shouldn&#39;t need an additional check for this condition.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Fill in the code for &lt;code&gt;isValidWord&lt;/code&gt; in &lt;code&gt;ps4a.py&lt;/code&gt; and be sure you&#39;ve passed the appropriate tests in &lt;code&gt;test_ps4a.py&lt;/code&gt; before pasting your function definition here.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;wrapper-problem-response&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34; aria-label=&#34;Question 1&#34; role=&#34;group&#34;&gt;&lt;div id=&#34;textbox_78fd656ca17b446e8096a6ab04198382_2_1&#34; class=&#34;capa_inputtype textbox cminput&#34;&gt;&lt;label class=&#34;sr problem-group-label&#34; for=&#34;cm-textarea-78fd656ca17b446e8096a6ab04198382_2_1&#34;&gt;Code Editor&lt;/label&gt;&lt;textarea rows=&#34;30&#34; cols=&#34;70&#34; name=&#34;input_78fd656ca17b446e8096a6ab04198382_2_1&#34; aria-label=&#34;python editor&#34; aria-describedby=&#34;answer_78fd656ca17b446e8096a6ab04198382_2_1&#34; id=&#34;input_78fd656ca17b446e8096a6ab04198382_2_1&#34; tabindex=&#34;0&#34; data-mode=&#34;python&#34; data-tabsize=&#34;4&#34; data-linenums=&#34;true&#34;&gt;def isValidWord(word, hand, wordList): &#34;&#34;&#34; Returns True if word is in the wordList and is entirely composed of letters in the hand. Otherwise, returns False. Does not mutate hand or wordList. word: string hand: dictionary (string -&amp;gt; int) wordList: list of lowercase strings &#34;&#34;&#34; i = 0 handCopy = hand.copy() for ch in word: if ch in handCopy.keys() and handCopy[ch] != 0: i += 1 handCopy[ch] -= 1 if len(word) == i and word in wordList: return True else: return False &lt;/textarea&gt;&lt;span class=&#34;cm-editor-exit-message Playing a Hand &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem-progress&#34; id=&#34;block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@problem+block@33dd64812fe2418e930ace3c3a465530-problem-progress&#34;&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem&#34;&gt; &lt;div&gt;&lt;style media=&#34;all&#34; type=&#34;text/css&#34;/&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;p&gt; In &lt;code&gt;ps4a.py&lt;/code&gt;, note that in the function &lt;code&gt;playHand&lt;/code&gt;, there is a bunch of &lt;i&gt;pseudocode&lt;/i&gt;. This pseudocode is provided to help guide you in writing your function. Check out the &lt;a href=&#34;//d37djvu3ytnwxt.cloudfront.net/assets/courseware/v1/85721a1199ca98dda55d8992bc93658d/asset-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@asset+block/WhyPseudocode.pdf&#34; target=&#34;_blank&#34;&gt;Why Pseudocode?&lt;/a&gt; resource to learn more about the What and Why of Pseudocode before you start coding your solution.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Note:&lt;/strong&gt; Do &lt;strong&gt;not&lt;/strong&gt; assume that there will always be 7 letters in a hand! The parameter &lt;code&gt;n&lt;/code&gt; represents the size of the hand. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Testing:&lt;/strong&gt; Before testing your code in the answer box, try out your implementation as if you were playing the game. Here is some example output of &lt;code&gt;playHand&lt;/code&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;section class=&#34;hints&#34;&gt;&lt;h3&gt;Test Cases&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;ht1l&#34;&gt;Case #1&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;ht1&#34;&gt; Function Call: &lt;pre&gt;wordList = loadWords() playHand({&#39;h&#39;:1, &#39;i&#39;:1, &#39;c&#39;:1, &#39;z&#39;:1, &#39;m&#39;:2, &#39;a&#39;:1}, wordList, 7)&lt;/pre&gt; Output: &lt;pre&gt; Current Hand: a c i h m m z Enter word, or a &#34;.&#34; to indicate that you are finished: him &#34;him&#34; earned 24 points. Total: 24 points Current Hand: a c m z Enter word, or a &#34;.&#34; to indicate that you are finished: cam &#34;cam&#34; earned 21 points. Total: 45 points Current Hand: z Enter word, or a &#34;.&#34; to indicate that you are finished: . Goodbye! Total score: 45 points. &lt;/pre&gt; &lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;ht2l&#34;&gt;Case #2&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;ht2&#34;&gt; Function Call: &lt;pre&gt;wordList = loadWords() playHand({&#39;w&#39;:1, &#39;s&#39;:1, &#39;t&#39;:2, &#39;a&#39;:1, &#39;o&#39;:1, &#39;f&#39;:1}, wordList, 7)&lt;/pre&gt; Output: &lt;pre&gt; Current Hand: a s t t w f o Enter word, or a &#34;.&#34; to indicate that you are finished: tow &#34;tow&#34; earned 18 points. Total: 18 points Current Hand: a s t f Enter word, or a &#34;.&#34; to indicate that you are finished: tasf Invalid word, please try again. Current Hand: a s t f Enter word, or a &#34;.&#34; to indicate that you are finished: fast &#34;fast&#34; earned 28 points. Total: 46 points Run out of letters. Total score: 46 points. &lt;/pre&gt; &lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;ht3l&#34;&gt;Case #3&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;ht3&#34;&gt; Function Call: &lt;pre&gt;wordList = loadWords() playHand({&#39;n&#39;:1, &#39;e&#39;:1, &#39;t&#39;:1, &#39;a&#39;:1, &#39;r&#39;:1, &#39;i&#39;:2}, wordList, 7)&lt;/pre&gt; Output: &lt;pre&gt; Current Hand: a r e t i i n Enter word, or a &#34;.&#34; to indicate that you are finished: inertia &#34;inertia&#34; earned 99 points. Total: 99 points Run out of letters. Total score: 99 points.&lt;/pre&gt; &lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;ht4l&#34;&gt;Additional Testing&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;ht4&#34;&gt; Be sure that, in addition to the listed tests, you test the same basic test conditions with varying values of &lt;code&gt;n&lt;/code&gt;. &lt;code&gt;n&lt;/code&gt; will never be smaller than the number of letters in the hand. &lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;br/&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;wrapper-problem-response&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34; aria-label=&#34;Question 1&#34; role=&#34;group&#34;&gt;&lt;div id=&#34;textbox_33dd64812fe2418e930ace3c3a465530_2_1&#34; class=&#34;capa_inputtype textbox cminput&#34;&gt;&lt;label class=&#34;sr problem-group-label&#34; for=&#34;cm-textarea-33dd64812fe2418e930ace3c3a465530_2_1&#34;&gt;Code Editor&lt;/label&gt;&lt;textarea rows=&#34;30&#34; cols=&#34;70&#34; name=&#34;input_33dd64812fe2418e930ace3c3a465530_2_1&#34; aria-label=&#34;python editor&#34; aria-describedby=&#34;answer_33dd64812fe2418e930ace3c3a465530_2_1&#34; id=&#34;input_33dd64812fe2418e930ace3c3a465530_2_1&#34; tabindex=&#34;0&#34; data-mode=&#34;python&#34; data-tabsize=&#34;4&#34; data-linenums=&#34;true&#34;&gt;def playHand(hand, wordList, n): &#34;&#34;&#34; Allows the user to play the given hand, as follows: * The hand is displayed. * The user may input a word or a single period (the string &#34;.&#34;) to indicate they&#39;re done playing * Invalid words are rejected, and a message is displayed asking the user to choose another word until they enter a valid word or &#34;.&#34; * When a valid word is entered, it uses up letters from the hand. * After every valid word: the score for that word is displayed, the remaining letters in the hand are displayed, and the user is asked to input another word. * The sum of the word scores is displayed when the hand finishes. * The hand finishes when there are no more unused letters or the user inputs a &#34;.&#34; hand: dictionary (string -&amp;gt; int) wordList: list of lowercase strings n: integer (HAND_SIZE; i.e., hand size required for additional points) &#34;&#34;&#34; total_score = 0 while sum(hand.values()) != 0: print(&#39;Current hand: &#39;, end = &#39; &#39;) displayHand(hand) print(&#39;Enter a word, or a &#34;.&#34; to indicate that you are finished: &#39;, end = &#34; &#34;) word = input() if word == &#39;.&#39;: break elif word != &#39;.&#39;: if isValidWord(word,hand,wordList) == False: print(&#39;Invalid word, please try again.&#39;) else: total_score += getWordScore(word, len(hand)) print(&#39;&#34;&#39; + word + &#39;&#34;&#39; + &#39; earned &#39; + str(getWordScore(word,len(hand))), end = &#34; &#34;) print(&#39;points.&#39; + &#39; Total: &#39; + str(total_score) + &#39; points&#39;) hand = updateHand(hand,word) print(&#39;Goodbye! Total score: &#39; +str(total_score) + &#39; points.&#39;) &lt;/textarea&gt;&lt;span class=&#34;cm-editor-exit-message capa-message&#34; id=&#34;cm-editor-exit-message-33dd64812fe2418e930ace3c3a465530_2_1&#34;&gt; Press ESC then TAB or click outside of the code editor to exit &lt;/span&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;grader-status&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34;&gt;&lt;span class=&#34;status correct&#34; id=&#34;status_33dd64812fe2418e930ace3c3a465530_2_1&#34; data-tooltip=&#34;This answer is correct.&#34;&gt;&lt;span class=&#34;sr&#34;&gt;correct&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class=&#34;status-icon&#34; aria-hidden=&#34;true&#34;/&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;p class=&#34;debug&#34;&gt;correct&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span id=&#34;answer_33dd64812fe2418e930ace3c3a465530_2_1&#34;/&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;external-grader-message&#34;&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;test&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;Test results&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;shortform&#34;&gt; CORRECT &lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;longform&#34;&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;result-output result-correct&#34;&gt;&lt;h4&gt;Function call: playHand({l: 1, m: 1, p: 1, u: 1})&#39;&amp;lt;edX internal wordList&amp;gt;&#39;, 4&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;p&gt;Test 1: Using all the letters in the hand on the first guess&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;dl&gt;&lt;dt&gt;Output:&lt;/dt&gt;&lt;dd class=&#34;result-actual-output&#34;&gt;&lt;pre&gt;Current hand: m l p u Enter a word, or a &#34;.&#34; to indicate that you are finished: plum &#34;plum&#34; earned 82 points. Total: 82 points Goodbye! Total score: 82 points. None &lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/dd&gt;&lt;/dl&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;result-output result-correct&#34;&gt;&lt;h4&gt;Function call: playHand({a: 1, z: 1})&#39;&amp;lt;edX internal wordList&amp;gt;&#39;, 2&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;p&gt;Test 2: Guessing incorrectly, then correctly&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;dl&gt;&lt;dt&gt;Output:&lt;/dt&gt;&lt;dd class=&#34;result-actual-output&#34;&gt;&lt;pre&gt;Current hand: z a Enter a word, or a &#34;.&#34; to indicate that you are finished: zo Invalid word, please try again. None &lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/dd&gt;&lt;/dl&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;result-output result-correct&#34;&gt;&lt;h4&gt;Function call: playHand({i: 1, o: 1, q: 1})&#39;&amp;lt;edX internal wordList&amp;gt;&#39;, 3&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;p&gt;Test 3: Guessing word, then quitting&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;dl&gt;&lt;dt&gt;Output:&lt;/dt&gt;&lt;dd class=&#34;result-actual-output&#34;&gt;&lt;pre&gt;Current hand: i o q Enter a word, or a &#34;.&#34; to indicate that you are finished: qi &#34;qi&#34; earned 22 points. Playing a Game &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem-progress&#34; id=&#34;block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@problem+block@c9fc61a418494ff6a456d160324fda91-problem-progress&#34;&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem&#34;&gt; &lt;div&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;p&gt;A game consists of playing multiple hands. We need to implement one final function to complete our word-game program. Write the code that implements the &lt;code&gt;playGame&lt;/code&gt; function. You should remove the code that is currently uncommented in the &lt;code&gt;playGame&lt;/code&gt; body. Read through the specification and make sure you understand what this function accomplishes. For the game, you should use the &lt;code&gt;HAND_SIZE&lt;/code&gt; constant to determine the number of cards in a hand.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;strong&gt;Testing:&lt;/strong&gt; Try out this implementation as if you were playing the game. Try out different values for &lt;code&gt;HAND_SIZE&lt;/code&gt; with your program, and be sure that you can play the wordgame with different hand sizes by modifying &lt;i&gt;only&lt;/i&gt; the variable &lt;code&gt;HAND_SIZE&lt;/code&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;section class=&#34;hints&#34;&gt;&lt;h3&gt;Sample Output&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;ht1l&#34;&gt;Here is how the game output should look...&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;ht1&#34;&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;code&gt; Loading word list from file... 83667 words loaded. Total: 99 points. Run out of letters. Total score: 99 points. Enter n to deal a new hand, r to replay the last hand, or e to end game: x Invalid command. Enter n to deal a new hand, r to replay the last hand, or e to end game: e &lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;ht2l&#34;&gt;Hints about the output&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;ht2&#34;&gt;&lt;p&gt;Be sure to inspect the above sample output carefully - very little is actually printed out in this function specifically. Most of the printed output actually comes from the code you wrote in &lt;code&gt;playHand&lt;/code&gt; - be sure that your code is modular and uses function calls to the &lt;code&gt;playHand&lt;/code&gt; helper function! &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;You should also make calls to the &lt;code&gt;dealHand&lt;/code&gt; helper function. You shouldn&#39;t make calls to any other helper function that we&#39;ve written so far - in fact, this function can be written in about 15-20 lines of code.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Here is the above output, with the output from &lt;code&gt;playHand&lt;/code&gt; obscured:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;pre&gt;&lt;code&gt; Loading word list from file... 83667 words loaded. Enter n to deal a new hand, r to replay the last hand, or e to end game: e &lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;p&gt;Hopefully this hint makes the problem seem a bit more approachable.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;ht3l&#34;&gt;Entering Your Code&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;ht3&#34;&gt;&lt;p&gt;Be sure to only paste your definition for &lt;code&gt;playGame&lt;/code&gt; in the following box. Do not include any other function definitions.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;ht4&#34;&gt;A Cool Trick about &#39;print&#39;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;ht4&#34;&gt;&lt;p&gt;A cool trick about &lt;code&gt;print&lt;/code&gt;: you can make two or more print statements print to the same line! Try out the following code. It will separate the first and second line with a space, and the second and third line with a &#34;?&#34; rather than putting each on a new line.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;pre&gt;print(&#39;Hello&#39;, end = &#34; &#34;) print(&#39;world&#39;, end=&#34;?&#34;) print(&#39;!&#39;)&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;br/&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;wrapper-problem-response&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34; aria-label=&#34;Question 1&#34; role=&#34;group&#34;&gt;&lt;div id=&#34;textbox_c9fc61a418494ff6a456d160324fda91_2_1&#34; class=&#34;capa_inputtype textbox cminput&#34;&gt;&lt;label class=&#34;sr problem-group-label&#34; for=&#34;cm-textarea-c9fc61a418494ff6a456d160324fda91_2_1&#34;&gt;Code Editor&lt;/label&gt;&lt;textarea rows=&#34;30&#34; cols=&#34;70&#34; name=&#34;input_c9fc61a418494ff6a456d160324fda91_2_1&#34; aria-label=&#34;python editor&#34; data-linenums=&#34;true&#34;&gt;def playGame(wordList): &#34;&#34;&#34; Allow the user to play an arbitrary number of hands. 1) Asks the user to input &#39;n&#39; or &#39;r&#39; or &#39;e&#39;. * If the user inputs &#39;n&#39;, let the user play a new (random) hand. * If the user inputs &#39;r&#39;, let the user play the last hand again. * If the user inputs &#39;e&#39;, exit the game. * If the user inputs anything else, tell them their input was invalid. 2) When done playing the hand, repeat from step 1 &#34;&#34;&#34; while True: print(&#39;Enter n to deal a new hand, r to replay the last hand, or e to end game:&#39;, end = &#34; &#34;) choice = input() try: if choice == &#39;n&#39;: n = HAND_SIZE hand = dealHand(HAND_SIZE) playHand(hand, wordList, n) elif choice == &#39;r&#39;: playHand(hand, wordList, n) elif choice == &#39;e&#39;: break else: print(&#39;Invalid command.&#39;) except UnboundLocalError: print(&#39;You have not played a hand yet. Please play a new hand first!&#39;) &lt;/textarea&gt;&lt;span class=&#34;cm-editor-exit-message capa-message&#34; id=&#34;cm-editor-exit-message-c9fc61a418494ff6a456d160324fda91_2_1&#34;&gt; Press ESC then TAB or click outside of the code editor to exit &lt;/span&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;grader-status&#34; class="edx-notes-wrapper-content"><p></p> <h3><span style="color: red;">**Part B is dependent on your functions from <code>ps4a.py</code>, so be sure to complete <code>ps4a.py</code> before working on <code>ps4b.py</code>**</span></h3> <p>Now that you have completed your word game code, you decide that you would like to enable your computer (SkyNet) to play the game (your hidden agenda is to prove once and for all that computers are inferior to human intellect!)&nbsp;In this part, you will be able to compare how you as a user succeed in the game compared to the computer's performance.</p> <p>You should look at the following two functions: <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier;">compChooseWord</span> and <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier;">compPlayHand</span>, before moving on to Problem 7 on the next page.</p> <h3><span style="font-family: 'Open Sans', Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; line-height: 25.6px;">compChooseWord</span></h3> <p>If you follow the pseudocode for <span style="font-family: 'courier new', courier;">compChooseWord</span>, you'll see that the code creates a computer player that is legal, but not always the best.&nbsp;Try to walk through and understand our implementation.</p> <p><strong><span style="font-family: 'Open Sans', Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">A Note On Runtime:&nbsp;</span></strong>You may notice that things run a bit slowly when the computer plays. This is to be expected - the <code>wordList</code> has 83667 words, after all!&nbsp;</p> <div class="collapsible"><header><strong>Test Cases to Understand the Code:&nbsp;</strong></header> <pre>&gt;&gt;&gt; compChooseWord({'a': 1, 'p': 2, 's': 1, 'e': 1, 'l': 1}, wordList, 6) appels &gt;&gt;&gt; compChooseWord({'a': 2, 'c': 1, 'b': 1, 't': 1}, wordList, 5) acta &gt;&gt;&gt; compChooseWord({'a': 2, 'e': 2, 'i': 2, 'm': 2, 'n': 2, 't': 2}, wordList, 12) immanent &gt;&gt;&gt; compChooseWord({'x': 2, 'z': 2, 'q': 2, 'n': 2, 't': 2}, wordList, 12) None</pre> <h3><span style="font-family: 'Open Sans', Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; line-height: 25.6px;">compPlayHand</span></h3> <p style="font-size: 16px; line-height: 25.6px;">Now that we have the ability to let the computer choose a word, we need to set up a function to allow the computer to play a hand - in a manner very similar to Part A's <code>playHand</code> function.&nbsp;This function allows the computer to play a given hand and is&nbsp;very similar to the earlier version in which a user selected the word, although deciding when it is done playing a particular hand is different.</p> <p><strong>Test Cases to Understand the Code:</strong>&nbsp;</p> <pre>compPlayHand({'a': 1, 'p': 2, 's': 1, 'e': 1, 'l': 1}, wordList, 6)</pre> <pre>Current Hand: a p p s e l</pre> <pre>"appels" earned 110 points. Total: 110 points</pre> <pre>Total score: 110 points.<br /><br /></pre> <pre></pre> <pre>compPlayHand({'a': 2, 'c': 1, 'b': 1, 't': 1}, wordList, 5)</pre> <pre>Current Hand: a a c b t "acta"&nbsp;</pre> <pre>earned 24 points. Total: 24 points&nbsp;</pre> <pre>Current Hand: b Total score: 24 points.&nbsp;<br /><br /></pre> <pre></pre> <pre>compPlayHand({'a': 2, 'e': 2, 'i': 2, 'm': 2, 'n': 2, 't': 2}, wordList, 12)</pre> <pre>Current Hand: a a e e i i m m n n t t</pre> <pre>"immanent" earned 96 points. Total: 96 points</pre> <pre>Current Hand: a e t i</pre> <pre>"ait" earned 9 points. Total: 105 points</pre> <pre>Current Hand: e</pre> <pre>Total score: 105 points.</pre> </div></div> </div> <script type="text/javascript"> (function (require) { You and your Computer &lt;/h3&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem-progress&#34; id=&#34;block-v1:MITx+6.00.1x+2T2017+type@problem+block@9ab07dc2c2c04de4a50e1b0c597f9d16-problem-progress&#34;&gt;&lt;/div&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem&#34;&gt; &lt;div&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;p&gt;Now that your computer can choose a word, you need to give the computer the option to play. Write the code that re-implements the &lt;code&gt;playGame&lt;/code&gt; function. You will modify the function to behave as described below in the function&#39;s comments. As before, you should use the &lt;code&gt;HAND_SIZE&lt;/code&gt; constant to determine the number of cards in a hand. Be sure to try out different values for &lt;code&gt;HAND_SIZE&lt;/code&gt; with your program.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;section class=&#34;hints&#34;&gt;&lt;h3&gt;Sample Output and Hints&lt;/h3&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;ht2&#34;&gt;Here is how the game output should look...&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;ht2&#34;&gt;&lt;pre&gt; Enter n to deal a new hand, r to replay the last hand, or e to end game: n Enter u to have yourself play, c to have the computer play: u Current Hand: a s r e t t t Enter word, or a &#34;.&#34; to indicate that you are finished: tatters &#34;tatters&#34; earned 99 points. Enter n to deal a new hand, r to replay the last hand, or e to end game: e &lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;ht3&#34;&gt;Hints about the output&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;ht3&#34;&gt;&lt;p&gt;Be sure to inspect the above sample output carefully - very little is actually printed out in this function specifically. Most of the printed output actually comes from the code you wrote in &lt;code&gt;playHand&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;compPlayHand&lt;/code&gt; - be sure that your code is modular and uses function calls to these helper functions! &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;You should also make calls to the &lt;code&gt;dealHand&lt;/code&gt; helper function. You shouldn&#39;t make calls to any other helper function that we&#39;ve written so far - in fact, this function can be written in about 15-20 lines of code.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Here is the above output, with the output from &lt;code&gt;playHand&lt;/code&gt; and &lt;code&gt;compPlayHand&lt;/code&gt; obscured:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;pre&gt; Enter n to deal a new hand, r to replay the last hand, or e to end game: r You have not played a hand yet. This is to be expected. If you want (totally optional!), feel free to investigate ways of making the computer&#39;s turn go faster - one way is to preprocess the word list into a dictionary (string -&amp;gt; int) so looking up the score of a word becomes much faster in the &lt;code&gt;compChooseWord&lt;/code&gt; function. &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Be careful though - you only want to do this preprocessing &lt;i&gt;one time&lt;/i&gt; - probably right after we generate the wordList for you (at the bottom of the file). If you choose to do this, you&#39;ll have to modify what inputs your functions take (they&#39;ll probably take a word dictionary instead of a word list, for example).&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;IMPORTANT:&lt;/b&gt;Don&#39;t worry about this issue when running your code in the checker below! We load a very small sample wordList (&lt;i&gt;much&lt;/i&gt; smaller than 83667 words!) to avoid having your code time out. Your code will work even if you don&#39;t implement a form of pre-processing as described.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;collapsible&#34;&gt;&lt;header&gt;&lt;a href=&#34;#&#34; id=&#34;ht4&#34;&gt;Entering Your Code&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/header&gt;&lt;section id=&#34;ht4&#34;&gt;&lt;p&gt;Be sure to only paste your definition for &lt;code&gt;playGame&lt;/code&gt; from &lt;code&gt;ps4b.py&lt;/code&gt; in the following box. Do not include any other function definitions.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/section&gt;&lt;br/&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;div class=&#34;wrapper-problem-response&#34; tabindex=&#34;-1&#34; aria-label=&#34;Question 1&#34; role=&#34;group&#34;&gt;&lt;div id=&#34;textbox_9ab07dc2c2c04de4a50e1b0c597f9d16_2_1&#34; class=&#34;capa_inputtype textbox cminput&#34;&gt;&lt;label class=&#34;sr problem-group-label&#34; for=&#34;cm-textarea-9ab07dc2c2c04de4a50e1b0c597f9d16_2_1&#34;&gt;Code Editor&lt;/label&gt;&lt;textarea rows=&#34;30&#34; cols=&#34;70&#34; name=&#34;input_9ab07dc2c2c04de4a50e1b0c597f9d16_2_1&#34; aria-label=&#34;python editor&#34; aria-describedby=&#34;answer_9ab07dc2c2c04de4a50e1b0c597f9d16_2_1&#34; id=&#34;input_9ab07dc2c2c04de4a50e1b0c597f9d16_2_1&#34; tabindex=&#34;0&#34; data-mode=&#34;python&#34; data-tabsize=&#34;4&#34; data-linenums=&#34;true&#34;&gt;def playGame(wordList): &#34;&#34;&#34; Allow the user to play an arbitrary number of hands. 1) Asks the user to input &#39;n&#39; or &#39;r&#39; or &#39;e&#39;. * If the user inputs &#39;e&#39;, immediately exit the game. * If the user inputs anything that&#39;s not &#39;n&#39;, &#39;r&#39;, or &#39;e&#39;, keep asking them again. 2) Asks the user to input a &#39;u&#39; or a &#39;c&#39;. * If the user inputs anything that&#39;s not &#39;c&#39; or &#39;u&#39;, keep asking them again. 3) Switch functionality based on the above choices: * If the user inputted &#39;n&#39;, play a new (random) hand. * Else, if the user inputted &#39;r&#39;, play the last hand again. But if no hand was played, output &#34;You have not played a hand yet. Please play a new hand first!&#34; * If the user inputted &#39;u&#39;, let the user play the game with the selected hand, using playHand. * If the user inputted &#39;c&#39;, let the computer play the game with the selected hand, using compPlayHand. 4) After the computer or user has played the hand, repeat from step 1 wordList: list (string) &#34;&#34;&#34; was_hand_played = False while True: while True: print(&#39;Enter n to deal a new hand, r to replay the last hand, or e to end game:&#39;, end = &#34; &#34;) choice = input() possible_choice = &#39;nre&#39; if choice not in possible_choice: print(&#39;Invalid command&#39;) elif choice == &#39;e&#39;: break elif choice == &#39;r&#39; and was_hand_played == False: print(&#39;You have not played a hand yet. Please play a new hand first!&#39;) else: break while True: if choice == &#39;e&#39;: break print(&#39;Enter u to have yourself play, c to have the computer play:&#39;, end = &#34; &#34;) choice_u_c = input() possible_choice_comp = &#39;uc&#39; if choice_u_c not in possible_choice_comp: print(&#39;Invalid command&#39;) else: break try: if choice == &#39;n&#39; and choice_u_c == &#39;u&#39;: n = HAND_SIZE hand = dealHand(HAND_SIZE) playHand(hand, wordList, n) elif choice == &#39;r&#39; and choice_u_c == &#39;u&#39;: playHand(hand, wordList, n) elif choice == &#39;e&#39;: break elif choice == &#39;n&#39; and choice_u_c == &#39;c&#39;: n = HAND_SIZE hand = dealHand(HAND_SIZE) compPlayHand(hand, wordList, n) elif choice == &#39;r&#39; and choice_u_c == &#39;c&#39;: compPlayHand(hand,wordList,n) else: print(&#39;Invalid command.&#39;) except UnboundLocalError: print(&#39;You have not played a hand yet. Computer Choosing a Word and Playing a Hand

**Part B is dependent on your functions from ps4a.py, so be sure to complete ps4a.py before working on ps4b.py**

Now that you have completed your word game code, you decide that you would like to enable your computer (SkyNet) to play the game (your hidden agenda is to prove once and for all that computers are inferior to human intellect!) In this part, you will be able to compare how you as a user succeed in the game compared to the computer's performance.

You should look at the following two functions: compChooseWord and compPlayHand, before moving on to Problem 7 on the next page.

compChooseWord

If you follow the pseudocode for compChooseWord, you'll see that the code creates a computer player that is legal, but not always the best. Try to walk through and understand our implementation.

A Note On Runtime: You may notice that things run a bit slowly when the computer plays. This is to be expected - the wordList has 83667 words, after all! 

Test Cases to Understand the Code: 
>>> compChooseWord({'a': 1, 'p': 2, 's': 1, 'e': 1, 'l': 1}, wordList, 6) 
appels 
>>> compChooseWord({'a': 2, 'c': 1, 'b': 1, 't': 1}, wordList, 5) 
acta 
>>> compChooseWord({'a': 2, 'e': 2, 'i': 2, 'm': 2, 'n': 2, 't': 2}, wordList, 12) 
immanent 
>>> compChooseWord({'x': 2, 'z': 2, 'q': 2, 'n': 2, 't': 2}, wordList, 12) 
None

compPlayHand

Now that we have the ability to let the computer choose a word, we need to set up a function to allow the computer to play a hand - in a manner very similar to Part A's playHand function. This function allows the computer to play a given hand and is very similar to the earlier version in which a user selected the word, although deciding when it is done playing a particular hand is different.

Test Cases to Understand the Code: 

compPlayHand({'a': 1, 'p': 2, 's': 1, 'e': 1, 'l': 1}, wordList, 6)
Current Hand: a p p s e l
"appels" earned 110 points. Total: 110 points
Total score: 110 points.



compPlayHand({'a': 2, 'c': 1, 'b': 1, 't': 1}, wordList, 5)


Current Hand: a a c b t "acta" 


earned 24 points. Total: 24 points 


Current Hand: b Total score: 24 points. 





compPlayHand({'a': 2, 'e': 2, 'i': 2, 'm': 2, 'n': 2, 't': 2}, wordList, 12)


Current Hand: a a e e i i m m n n t t


"immanent" earned 96 points. Total: 96 points


Current Hand: a e t i


"ait" earned 9 points. Total: 105 points


Current Hand: e


Total score: 105 points.
